5:["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"The Bitter Lesson is Sutton's argument that, over the long run, general methods that scale with compute and data outperform systems built around hand-crafted domain knowledge. It is a historical pattern claim, not a theorem, and its force comes from repeated examples in search, game playing, vision, and language."}]

da:["$","li","low-rank-adaptation-lora",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/low-rank-adaptation-lora","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Low-Rank Adaptation (LoRA)"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"LoRA fine-tunes a model by expressing each weight update as a low-rank product \\( \\Delta W = BA \\) while keeping the original weight matrix frozen. 199:["$","li","state-space-models-mamba",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/state-space-models-mamba","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"State Space Models / Mamba"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A family of sequence models that evolve a hidden state through a linear recurrence \\( h_t = \\bar{A} h_{t-1} + \\bar{B} x_t \\), \\( y_t = C h_t \\), making them RNN-like at inference yet convolutional and parallel at training. Mamba (Gu &amp; Dao, 2023) added input-dependent (\"selective\") transitions and an efficient hardware-aware scan, turning SSMs into competitive Transformer alternatives with linear complexity in sequence length."}]]}]}]

Although lossy compared to softmax attention, linear attention is central to efficient Transformers (Performer, Linear Transformer) and deeply related to modern State Space Models."}]]}]}]
19b:["$","li","alibi-attention-with-linear-biases",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/alibi-attention-with-linear-biases","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"ALiBi (Attention with Linear Biases)"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A positional encoding for Transformers that adds a static, head-specific linear penalty \\( -m_h \\cdot (i - j) \\) directly into the attention logits, replacing sinusoidal or learned positional embeddings. Its training-free length extrapolation property — models trained on 1K tokens evaluate well on much longer sequences — made ALiBi influential before RoPE + NTK-style scaling took over."}]]}]}]
19c:["$","li","yarn-ntk-aware-rope-scaling",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/yarn-ntk-aware-rope-scaling","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"YaRN / NTK-aware RoPE Scaling"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A family of techniques for extending the usable context length of a RoPE-based Transformer beyond its training length by <i>re-parameterising</i> the rotary frequencies rather than retraining from scratch. 19d:["$","li","sliding-window-attention",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/sliding-window-attention","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Sliding-Window Attention"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"An attention pattern that restricts each query to attend only within a local window of the last \\( w \\) tokens, reducing the cost per query from \\( O(T) \\) to \\( O(w) \\) and the KV cache from \\( O(T) \\) to \\( O(w) \\) per layer. Combined with global tokens (Longformer), dilated windows (BigBird), or a few full-attention layers (Mistral), it is a ubiquitous tool for scaling Transformers to long contexts without abandoning softmax attention entirely."}]]}]}]

1f4:["$","li","positive-semi-definite-matrices",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/positive-semi-definite-matrices","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Positive (Semi-)Definite Matrices"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A symmetric matrix \\( A \\in \\mathbb{R}^{n \\times n} \\) is positive semi-definite (PSD) if \\( x^\\top A x \\ge 0 \\) for all \\( x \\), and positive definite (PD) if strict for \\( x \\ne 0 \\). It controls PAC generalisation: if \\( \\text{VC}(\\mathcal{H}) = d \\), then with probability \\( 1 - \\delta \\) all \\( h \\in \\mathcal{H} \\) satisfy \\( L(h) \\le \\hat L(h) + O(\\sqrt{d/n}) \\). 207:["$","li","rademacher-complexity",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/rademacher-complexity","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Rademacher Complexity"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"The empirical Rademacher complexity of a function class \\( \\mathcal{F} \\) on data \\( S = (z_1, \\dots, z_n) \\) is \\( \\hat{\\mathfrak{R}}_S(\\mathcal{F}) = \\mathbb{E}_\\sigma[\\sup_{f \\in \\mathcal{F}} \\tfrac{1}{n}\\sum_i \\sigma_i f(z_i)] \\) — the expected ability of \\( \\mathcal{F} \\) to correlate with random \\( \\pm 1 \\) signs. 208:["$","li","no-free-lunch-theorem",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/no-free-lunch-theorem","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"No-Free-Lunch Theorem"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Averaged over all possible target functions or data distributions, every learning algorithm performs identically. Any algorithm's superiority on one class of problems must be paid for by inferior performance on another. NFL is not a practical barrier — real-world problems occupy a tiny, structured subset — but it is the theoretical basis for why <i>inductive bias</i> is a first-class design choice, not an implementation detail."}]]}]}]
209:["$","li","goodharts-law-and-specification-gaming",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/goodharts-law-and-specification-gaming","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Goodhart's Law and Specification Gaming"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"When a measure becomes a target, it ceases to be a good measure. Optimising a proxy metric \\( \\hat{M} \\) for a true-but-unobservable goal \\( M \\) tends to decouple them once optimisation pressure is strong enough. Specification gaming is the RL-specific manifestation: agents maximise reward by exploiting the reward specification rather than achieving the intended behaviour. These twin failure modes underlie most benchmark-gaming, reward-hacking, and evaluation-contamination stories in modern ML."}]]}]}]

21c:["$","li","gpu-memory-hierarchy-and-roofline-model",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/gpu-memory-hierarchy-and-roofline-model","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"GPU Memory Hierarchy and the Roofline Model"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Modern GPUs have a layered memory hierarchy: HBM (high-bandwidth global, ~1–3 TB/s), L2 cache, SRAM / shared memory per SM (~20 TB/s), and registers. The representer theorem says that the minimiser of any regularised empirical risk lies in the span of kernel evaluations on the training points — reducing infinite-dimensional optimisation to \\( n \\) coefficients."}]]}]}]
22c:["$","li","mercers-theorem-kernel-feature-maps",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/mercers-theorem-kernel-feature-maps","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Mercer's Theorem & Kernel Feature Maps"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Mercer's theorem: any continuous, symmetric, positive semi-definite kernel \\( k(x, y) \\) on a compact domain admits an eigendecomposition \\( k(x, y) = \\sum_i \\lambda_i \\phi_i(x) \\phi_i(y) \\). 297:["$","li","loss-landscape-visualization",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/loss-landscape-visualization","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Loss Landscape Visualization"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Methods for visualising high-dimensional loss surfaces by projecting parameters onto 1-D or 2-D subspaces. 298:["$","li","gradient-surgery-pcgrad",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/gradient-surgery-pcgrad","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Gradient Surgery (PCGrad) for Multi-Task Learning"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"When two task gradients in multi-task learning point in conflicting directions (negative cosine), they partially cancel each other and slow learning. 299:["$","li","contrastive-learning-theory",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/contrastive-learning-theory","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Contrastive Learning Theory"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"The theoretical account of why contrastive self-supervised objectives like InfoNCE produce useful representations. Wang & Isola (2020) show the InfoNCE loss decomposes into two asymptotic terms — \\( \\mathcal{L}_{\\text{align}} \\), pulling positive pairs together, and \\( \\mathcal{L}_{\\text{unif}} \\), spreading the marginal feature distribution uniformly on the hypersphere. The downstream linear-probe accuracy correlates almost perfectly with this alignment-uniformity trade-off, giving a geometric explanation for why contrastive learning works at all."}]]}]}]
29a:["$","li","non-contrastive-ssl",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/non-contrastive-ssl","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Non-Contrastive SSL (BYOL, SimSiam, Barlow Twins, VICReg)"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Self-supervised methods that learn from positive pairs alone — no negatives — and yet do not collapse to a constant. BYOL (Grill et al. 2020) and SimSiam (Chen & He 2021) achieve this by an asymmetric architecture: a predictor MLP on one branch and a stop-gradient on the other. Barlow Twins (Zbontar et al. 2021) and VICReg (Bardes et al. 2022) instead enforce non-collapse explicitly via a feature covariance regulariser. The common theme is replacing the contrastive uniformity term by an architectural or statistical anti-collapse mechanism."}]]}]}]
29b:["$","li","disentangled-representation-learning",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/disentangled-representation-learning","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Disentangled Representation Learning"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"The pursuit of latent variables \\( z = (z_1, \\ldots, z_d) \\) whose components correspond to independent semantic factors of variation (pose, identity, lighting). β-VAE (Higgins et al. 2017) up-weights the KL term in the VAE ELBO to encourage axis-aligned independent posteriors; FactorVAE (Kim & Mnih 2018) penalises the total correlation directly. Locatello et al. (2019) prove that fully unsupervised disentanglement is impossible without inductive biases, reframing the field around weak supervision and benchmark-driven evaluation."}]]}]}]
29c:["$","li","sparse-representations-in-deep-nets",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/sparse-representations-in-deep-nets","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Sparse Representations in Deep Nets"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Modern deep networks naturally produce sparse activations: ReLU networks have median activation sparsity \\( \\sim 50\\% \\); transformer MLPs reach \\( 80–95\\% \\) per-token sparsity in late layers. Sparsity is a free regulariser, an exploitable inference acceleration target, and a theoretical lens — the lottery-ticket hypothesis (Frankle & Carbin 2019) shows dense networks contain sparse subnetworks that train to full accuracy in isolation. Recent work (Mirzadeh et al. 2024, Liu et al. 2023) leverages activation sparsity for 2–10× LLM inference speedups via top-k routing."}]]}]}]
29d:["$","li","representation-collapse",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/representation-collapse","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Representation Collapse"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A failure mode of representation learning where the encoder produces low-rank or constant features, eliminating useful signal. Three common modes: <b>complete collapse</b> (\\( f \\equiv c \\), seen in non-contrastive SSL without anti-collapse mechanisms), <b>dimensional collapse</b> (Jing et al. 2022 — features span a low-dimensional subspace), and <b>neural collapse</b> (Papyan, Han & Donoho 2020 — late-training features cluster onto class-mean simplex). Each mode has distinct diagnostics (feature variance, eigenspectrum decay, simplex angle) and distinct mitigations."}]]}]}]
29e:["$","li","invariance-vs-equivariance",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/invariance-vs-equivariance","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Invariance vs Equivariance"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"A representation \\( f: X \\to Z \\) is <i>invariant</i> to a group action \\( g \\in G \\) if \\( f(g \\cdot x) = f(x) \\), and <i>equivariant</i> if \\( f(g \\cdot x) = \\rho_Z(g) \\cdot f(x) \\) for some representation \\( \\rho_Z \\) of \\( G \\) on \\( Z \\). Invariance throws away the group's information; equivariance preserves it in a structured form. Choosing one over the other depends on whether the downstream task needs to recover the group element. CNNs are translation-equivariant; group-equivariant CNNs (Cohen & Welling 2016) extend this to rotations, reflections, and beyond."}]]}]}]
29f:["$","li","embedding-geometry",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/embedding-geometry","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Embedding Geometry"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"The geometry of learned vector representations — how distance, angle, and clustering structure encode semantics. Word2vec produced the famous parallelogram \\( \\vec{\\text{king}} - \\vec{\\text{man}} + \\vec{\\text{woman}} \\approx \\vec{\\text{queen}} \\) (Mikolov et al. 2013). Modern embeddings exhibit anisotropy — token embeddings cluster in narrow cones — addressed by whitening and isotropy-promoting losses. Cosine similarity dominates as the standard metric because magnitude in trained embeddings often confounds frequency rather than semantics."}]]}]}]
2a0:["$","li","metric-learning-at-scale",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/metric-learning-at-scale","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Metric Learning at Scale"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Metric learning trains an encoder so that distances in embedding space match a semantic similarity. At billion-vector scale (web search, face identification, ad recommendation), the bottleneck shifts from loss design to nearest-neighbour data structures (HNSW, IVF-PQ in FAISS), product quantization for index compression, and hard-negative mining strategies that don't blow up training cost. 2a1:["$","li","representation-alignment-across-modalities",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/representation-alignment-across-modalities","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Representation Alignment Across Modalities"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Cross-modal alignment trains separate encoders for different input types (image, text, audio) so that paired examples land near each other in a shared embedding space. CLIP (Radford et al. 2021) uses a symmetric InfoNCE on \\( 4 \\times 10^8 \\) image–text pairs from the web, learning a joint space where zero-shot image classification is performed by similarity to a text prototype. The geometry of the joint space is the entire interface between modalities — downstream tasks (retrieval, classification, generation guidance) operate on this aligned embedding rather than on raw pixels or tokens."}]]}]}]
2a2:["$","li","tokenization-as-representation",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/tokenization-as-representation","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Tokenization as Representation"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Tokenization is a representation choice, not a preprocessing detail — it determines what the model can and cannot see. 2a3:["$","li","autoregressive-vs-diffusion-tradeoffs",{"className":"wiki-topic-list-item","children":["$","$L3",null,{"href":"/ml/wiki/autoregressive-vs-diffusion-tradeoffs","className":"wiki-topic-list-link","children":[["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-title","children":"Autoregressive vs Diffusion Tradeoffs"}],["$","span",null,{"className":"wiki-topic-list-summary","children":"Autoregressive models factorise \\( p(x) = \\prod_t p(x_t \\mid x_{<t}) \\) and dominate text generation; diffusion models learn a denoising process and dominate continuous-modality generation. The two paradigms differ in likelihood tractability, sampling cost, controllability, and compositionality — and the right choice depends on whether tokens are discrete, parallel decoding is required, and whether log-likelihood or perceptual quality is the figure of merit."}]]}]}]
